intermediate
6 min
The Intellect's Property: Knowing Universals Through Particulars
Ibn Taymiyya defines the intellect's property as knowing universals through particulars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Ibn Taymiyya's conception of the intellect's property (خاصة العقل) and contrast it with the logicians' view that universals can be known independently of particulars.

Core Idea
The intellect's distinctive function is to abstract universals from particular experiences.

Ibn Taymiyya devotes a key part of his argument to defining the nature of the intellect. He asserts that 'the property of the intellect is its knowledge of universals through its knowledge of particulars.' This lesson examines that claim and its implications for how we acquire knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Locate the phrase 'خاصة العقل'
Find the sentence in the Arabic where Ibn Taymiyya defines the intellect's property. It is after he asks how mentioning particulars can weaken the syllogism.
The exact phrase: 'فإن خاصة العقل معرفته الكليات بتوسط معرفته بالجزئيات'
2
Translate and interpret the definition
Translate: 'the property of the intellect is its knowledge of universals through its knowledge of particulars.' What does 'through' mean here? It implies mediation.
The intellect does not directly know universals; it needs particular experiences first.
3
Identify the logicians' opposing view
Ibn Taymiyya says whoever denies this property denies the intellect itself. Whom is he accusing? The logicians who claim examples weaken reasoning implicitly deny this property.
He calls those who think mentioning particulars without examples is stronger as 'obstinate' (مكابر).
4
Connect to his overall argument
How does this definition support his claim that examples strengthen knowledge? If the intellect needs particulars, then providing examples (particulars) is essential.
Examples are not extraneous; they are the raw material for abstraction.
5
Apply to an Islamic science
In tafsir, how do mufassirun use specific verses to derive universal principles? For instance, from the story of Adam (specific) they derive the principle of repentance (universal).
This mirrors the intellect's operation.

المقام الرابع - الوجه السابع : ذكر الأصل لتنبيه العقل على المشترك الكلي المشترك مع بعض أفراده أثبتُ في العقل من ذكره مجرداً عن جميع الأفراد باتفاق العقلاء. ولهذا هم يقولون : إن العقل بحسب إحساسه [٣٥٨] بالجزئيات يدرك العقل بينها قدراً مشتركاً كلياً. فالكليات في النفس تقع بعد معرفة الجزئيات المعيَّنة. فمعرفة الكليات الجزئيات المعينة من أعظم الأسباب في معرفة الكليات فكيف يكون ذكرها مضعفاً للقياس، ويكون عدم ذكرها موجباً لقوته؟ وهذه خاصة العقل، فإن خاصة العقل معرفته الكليات بتوسط معرفته بالجزئيات فمن أنكرها أنكر خاصة عقل الإنسان، ومن جعل ذكرها بدون شيء من محالها المعينة أقوى من ذكرها مع التمثيل لمواضعها المعينة كان مكابراً. والعقلاء باتفاقهم يعلمون أن ضرب المثل الكلي مما يعين على معرفته، وأنه ليس الحال إذا ذكر مع المثال كالحال إذا ذكر مجرداً عن المثال . ومن تدبر جميع ما يتكلم فيه الناس من الكليات المعلومة بالعقل في الطب، أمثلة لكلية انجذاب النظير والحساب والطبيعيات والصناعات والتجارات وغير ذلك، وجد الأمر كذلك. فإذا قيل : يَسْخُن جوف الإنسان في الشتاء ويبرد في الصيف، لأنه في الشتاء يكون الهواء بارداً فيبرد ظاهرُ البدن فتهرب الحرارة إلى باطن البدن، لأن الضد يهرب من الضد، والنظير ينجذب إلى شبيهه، فتظهر البرودة إلى الظاهر، لأن شبيه الشيء منجذب إليه - كان هذا أمراً كلياً مطلقاً فإذا قيل : ولهذا يَسْخُن جوفُ الأرض في الشتاء، [٣٥٩] وجوف الحيوان كله، ولهذا تبرد الأجواف في الصيف لسخونة الظواهر فتهرب البرودة إلى الأجواف - كان كلما تصور الإنسان النظائر قويت معرفته بتلك الكلية، وهو أن الضد يهرب من ضده والنظير ينجذب إلى نظيره. وهذا معلوم في الطبيعيات والنفسانيات وغيرهما. لكن إذا ذكرت النظائر قوي العلم بذلك. وقد يعبر عن ذلك بأن «الجنسية علة القم. [احتمال: علة الحب]». وكذلك إذا قيل : الشمس إذا وقعت على البحر أو غيره سَخَّنته فتصاعد منه بخار، مثال تصاعد البخار لأن الحرارة تحلل الرطوبة. ثم قيل : كما يتصاعد البخار من القدر التي فيها الماء الحار - / كان هذا المثال مما يؤكد معرفة الأول. والأقيسة التي يستعملها الفلاسفة في علومهم ويجعلونها كلية كلُّها يعتضدون فيها على الشاهد بالأمثلة. وليس مع القوم إلا ما علموه من صفات الأمور المشاهدة، ثم قاسوا الغائب على المشاهدة به بالجامع المشترك الذي يجعلونه كلياً. فإن لم يكن هذا صحيحاً لم يكن مع أحد من أهل الأرض علم كلي يشترك فيه ما شهده وما غاب عنه، حتى قوله : «الخبز يشبع و الماء يروي ونحو ذلك . فإنه لم يعلم بحسه إلا أموراً معينة، فمن أين له أن الغائب بمنزلة الشاهد إلا بهذه الطريق؟ والإنسان قد ينكر أمراً حتى يرى واحداً جنسه ، فيقر بالنوع ويستفيد بذلك حكماً كلياً. ولهذا يقول سبحانه: ﴿ كَذَّبَتْ قَوْمُ [٣٦٠] نُوحٍ الْمُرْسَلِينَ، كَذَبَتْ عَادُ الْمُرْسَلِينَ، كَذَّبَتْ ثَمُودُ الْمُرْسَلِينَ ﴾ ، ونحو ذلك . وكلّ من هؤلاء إنما جاءه رسول واحد، لكن كانوا مكذبين بجنس الرسل بجنس الرُّسل لم يكن تكذيبهم بالواحد لخصوصه. وهذا بخلاف تكذيب اليهود والنصارى لمحمد صلى الله عليه وسلم فإنهم لم يكذبوا جنس الرسل، إنما كَذَّبوا واحداً بعينه. بخلاف مشركي العرب الذين لم يعرفوا الرسل، فإن الله يحتج عليهم في القرآن بإثبات جنس الرسالة . ولهذا يجيب سبحانه عن شُبَهِ منكري جنس الرسالة كقولهم : لو أَبَعَثَ الله بشرا رسولا [سورة الإسراء : ٩٤]، فيقول : ﴿وَمَا أَرْسَلْنَا مِن قَبْلِكَ إِلَّا رِجَالًا نُوحِيَ إِلَيْهِمْ فَسْتَلُوا أَهْلَ الذِكرِ إِن كُنتُمْ لَا تَعْلَمُونَ ﴾ [سورة النحل : ٤٣] . أي هذا متواتر عند أهل الكتاب، فاسئلوهم عن الرسل الذين جاءتهم أكانوا بشراً أم لا؟». وكذلك قوله : ﴿ وَقَالُوا لَوْلَا أُنزِلَ عَلَيْهِ مَلَكُ وَلَوْ أَنزَلْنَا مَلَكًا لَّقُضِيَ الْأَمْرُ ثُمَّ لَا يُنظَرُونَ ) وَلَوْ جَعَلْنَهُ مَلَكًا لَّجَعَلْتَهُ رَجُلًا وَلَلَبَسْنَا عَلَيْهِم مَّا يَلْبِسُونَ ﴾ [سورة الأنعام: ۸ - ۹] . فإنهم لا يُطيقون الأخذ عن الملك في صورته ، فلو أرسلنا إليهم مَلَكاً لجعلناه رجلاً في صورة الإنسان، وحينئذ كان يلتبس عليهم الأمرُ ويقولون هو رجل ، والرجل لا يكون رسولاً». وكذلك الرسل قبله. قال تعالى : ( أَوَعَبْتُمْ أَن جَاءَكُمْ ذِكْرٌ مِّن رَّبِّكُمْ عَلَى رَجُلٍ مِّنكُمْ لِيُنذِرَكُمْ) [سورة الأعراف : ٦٣] ، كما قال [٣٦١] تعالى: ﴿ أَكَانَ لِلنَّاسِ عَجَبًا أَنْ أَوْحَيْنَا إِلَى رَجُلٍ مِّنْهُمْ أَنْ أَنذِرِ النَّاسَ ﴾ [سورة يونس : ٢] وكما قال تعالى: ﴿قُلْ مَا كُنتُ بِدْعَا مِنَ الرُّسُلِ ﴾ [سورة الأحقاف: ٩]، ونحو ذلك.
The fourth station - the seventh aspect: Mentioning the principle to alert the intellect to the universal common. The universal common with some of its individuals is more established in the intellect than mentioning it devoid of all individuals, by agreement of the rational people. And therefore they say: The intellect, by virtue of its sensation of particulars, perceives among them a common universal quantity. So universals occur in the soul after knowledge of specific particulars. Knowledge of universals through specific particulars is among the greatest causes for knowledge of universals; so how can mentioning them weaken the syllogism, and not mentioning them be a cause for its strength? And this is a property of the intellect, for the property of the intellect is its knowledge of universals through its knowledge of particulars. So whoever denies this denies the property of the human intellect, and whoever makes mentioning them without any of their specific instances stronger than mentioning them with exemplification of their specific loci is being obstinate. The rational people unanimously know that striking a universal example assists in its knowledge, and that the case when it is mentioned with an example is not like the case when it is mentioned without an example. And whoever ponders all that people speak of regarding universals known by the intellect in medicine, examples for the universal of attraction of like and calculation and natural sciences and crafts and trades and other than that, finds the matter so. So if it is said: The interior of man becomes hot in winter and cold in summer, because in winter the air is cold so the exterior of the body cools and the heat flees to the interior of the body, for the opposite flees from the opposite, and the like is attracted to its similar, so coldness appears to the exterior because the similar of a thing is attracted to it - this would be an absolute universal matter. Then if it is said: Therefore the interior of the earth becomes hot in winter, and the interior of all animals, and therefore the interiors become cold in summer due to the heat of the exteriors so the coldness flees to the interiors - then whenever a person imagines the similars, his knowledge of that universal strengthens, i.e., that the opposite flees from its opposite and the like is attracted to its like. And this is known in natural and psychological matters and others. But when the similars are mentioned, knowledge of that is strengthened. And this is sometimes expressed by 'Homogeneity is the cause of [love?]'. Likewise, if it is said: The sun when it falls on the sea or other than it heats it so steam rises from it, an example of the rising of steam because heat dissolves moisture. Then it is said: Just as steam rises from the pot containing hot water - then this example strengthens knowledge of the first. And the syllogisms that the philosophers use in their sciences and make them universal - all of them they seek support in them by sensory evidence with examples. And the people have nothing except what they know of the attributes of observed matters, then they analogize the absent to the observed by the common factor that they make universal. For if this were not correct, there would be with no one on earth a universal knowledge that encompasses what he observed and what is absent from him, even his statement: 'Bread satiates and water quenches' and so on. For he only knows by his sensation specific matters; so from where does he have that the absent is like the observed except by this method? And a person may deny a matter until he sees one of its kind, then he acknowledges the type and thereby benefits a universal judgment. And therefore Allah Almighty says: 'The people of Noah denied the messengers, 'Ad denied the messengers, Thamud denied the messengers' and so on. And each of these was only sent one messenger, but they were deniers of the genus of messengers; their denial was not of the one for his specificity. This is unlike the denial of the Jews and Christians of Muhammad صلى الله عليه وسلم, for they did not deny the genus of messengers, they only denied one specific one. Unlike the polytheist Arabs who did not know messengers, for Allah argues against them in the Qur'an by establishing the genus of messengerhood. And therefore He answers the doubts of the deniers of the genus of messengerhood, like their statement: 'If Allah had sent a human as a messenger' [Surah al-Isra 94], He says 'And We sent not before you except men whom We inspired - so ask the people of remembrance if you do not know' [Surah al-Nahl 43]. That is, this is mutawatir among the People of the Book, so ask them about the messengers who came to them, were they human or not? And likewise His statement: 'And they said: Why was there not sent down to him an angel? And if We had sent down an angel, the matter would have been decided and then they would not be reprieved. And if We had made him an angel, We would have made him a man and We would have confused for them what they confuse' [Surah al-An'am 8-9]. For they cannot receive from an angel in its form; if We had sent them an angel, We would have made him a man in the form of a human, and then the matter would be confused for them and they would say he is a man, and a man cannot be a messenger. And likewise the messengers before him. He said: 'Is it a wonder for people that We inspired a man from among them to warn the people?' [Surah Yunus 2]. And as He said: 'Say: I am not an innovation among the messengers' [Surah al-Ahqaf 9], and so on.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage is a critical argument against the logicians' claim that mentioning examples weakens the syllogism. Ibn Taymiyya opens by stating that a universal common (المشترك الكلي) when accompanied by some of its individuals is more firmly established in the intellect than when mentioned in isolation. He then explains that the intellect grasps universals by first sensing particulars; thus, universals follow knowledge of specific individuals. Therefore, mentioning particulars cannot weaken the syllogism; rather, it strengthens it. He calls those who claim the opposite as obstinate (مكابر). He provides examples from natural phenomena: the movement of heat and cold in bodies, and the rise of steam from heated water. He also cites the use of examples in various fields like medicine, calculation, and crafts. Next, he argues that the philosophers' syllogisms rely on observed examples; all universal knowledge depends on extrapolating from the observed to the absent. Without this method, even basic knowledge like 'bread satiates' would be impossible. Finally, he uses a scriptural example: the denial of a single messenger by past nations constitutes denial of the genus of messengers (جنس الرسل), showing that the universal genus is known through the particular instance. This reinforces his point that universal knowledge is achieved through particulars and examples.

خاصة العقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, what is the property of the intellect (خاصة العقل)?
A) It knows universals independently of particulars.
B) It knows universals through knowledge of particulars.
C) It only knows particulars.
D) It creates universals from nothing.

Key Takeaway
The intellect's distinctive function is to derive universal concepts from particular experiences; denying this is to deny the intellect itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: Take a universal concept from 'aqidah, such as 'mercy' (رحمة). Describe how you would illustrate this universal using particular examples from the Qur'an (e.g., Allah's mercy to the prophets, believers, and even non-believers). Explain how these particulars strengthen your understanding of the universal.

intermediate
7 min
The Dependence of Syllogisms on Observed Examples
Ibn Taymiyya argues that all syllogisms depend on observed examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze Ibn Taymiyya's argument that all universal syllogisms, even those used by philosophers, ultimately rely on observed examples.

Core Idea
Every universal statement, including 'bread satiates', is known only by extrapolating from observed particulars.

Ibn Taymiyya delivers a powerful critique: if the logicians claim that examples weaken syllogisms, then even the most basic universal knowledge—like bread satiating—would be impossible. He shows that all reasoning, no matter how abstract, depends on sensory experience.

Guided Path
1
Find the challenge to the logicians
Locate the part where Ibn Taymiyya asks about 'bread satiates' and 'water quenches'. He uses this as an example of universal knowledge that everyone relies on.
He argues that even such simple knowledge is derived from observing specific instances.
2
Understand his reasoning
He says: 'He only knows by his sensation specific matters; so from where does he have that the absent is like the observed except by this method?' This shows that universals require extrapolation.
The method is analogical reasoning from observed to unobserved.
3
Identify the common factor (الجامع)
The philosophers' syllogisms rely on a 'common factor' (الجامع المشترك) that they make universal. This common factor is what links the observed to the absent.
Without this common factor, no universal conclusion can be drawn.
4
Apply to a fiqhi example
In fiqh, the 'illah (effective cause) serves as the common factor. For instance, intoxication is the common factor that links wine and nabidh, allowing the prohibition to be extended.
This mirrors the logical method Ibn Taymiyya describes.

المقام الرابع - الوجه السابع : ذكر الأصل لتنبيه العقل على المشترك الكلي المشترك مع بعض أفراده أثبتُ في العقل من ذكره مجرداً عن جميع الأفراد باتفاق العقلاء. ولهذا هم يقولون : إن العقل بحسب إحساسه [٣٥٨] بالجزئيات يدرك العقل بينها قدراً مشتركاً كلياً. فالكليات في النفس تقع بعد معرفة الجزئيات المعيَّنة. فمعرفة الكليات الجزئيات المعينة من أعظم الأسباب في معرفة الكليات فكيف يكون ذكرها مضعفاً للقياس، ويكون عدم ذكرها موجباً لقوته؟ وهذه خاصة العقل، فإن خاصة العقل معرفته الكليات بتوسط معرفته بالجزئيات فمن أنكرها أنكر خاصة عقل الإنسان، ومن جعل ذكرها بدون شيء من محالها المعينة أقوى من ذكرها مع التمثيل لمواضعها المعينة كان مكابراً. والعقلاء باتفاقهم يعلمون أن ضرب المثل الكلي مما يعين على معرفته، وأنه ليس الحال إذا ذكر مع المثال كالحال إذا ذكر مجرداً عن المثال . ومن تدبر جميع ما يتكلم فيه الناس من الكليات المعلومة بالعقل في الطب، أمثلة لكلية انجذاب النظير والحساب والطبيعيات والصناعات والتجارات وغير ذلك، وجد الأمر كذلك. فإذا قيل : يَسْخُن جوف الإنسان في الشتاء ويبرد في الصيف، لأنه في الشتاء يكون الهواء بارداً فيبرد ظاهرُ البدن فتهرب الحرارة إلى باطن البدن، لأن الضد يهرب من الضد، والنظير ينجذب إلى شبيهه، فتظهر البرودة إلى الظاهر، لأن شبيه الشيء منجذب إليه - كان هذا أمراً كلياً مطلقاً فإذا قيل : ولهذا يَسْخُن جوفُ الأرض في الشتاء، [٣٥٩] وجوف الحيوان كله، ولهذا تبرد الأجواف في الصيف لسخونة الظواهر فتهرب البرودة إلى الأجواف - كان كلما تصور الإنسان النظائر قويت معرفته بتلك الكلية، وهو أن الضد يهرب من ضده والنظير ينجذب إلى نظيره. وهذا معلوم في الطبيعيات والنفسانيات وغيرهما. لكن إذا ذكرت النظائر قوي العلم بذلك. وقد يعبر عن ذلك بأن «الجنسية علة القم. [احتمال: علة الحب]». وكذلك إذا قيل : الشمس إذا وقعت على البحر أو غيره سَخَّنته فتصاعد منه بخار، مثال تصاعد البخار لأن الحرارة تحلل الرطوبة. ثم قيل : كما يتصاعد البخار من القدر التي فيها الماء الحار - / كان هذا المثال مما يؤكد معرفة الأول. والأقيسة التي يستعملها الفلاسفة في علومهم ويجعلونها كلية كلُّها يعتضدون فيها على الشاهد بالأمثلة. وليس مع القوم إلا ما علموه من صفات الأمور المشاهدة، ثم قاسوا الغائب على المشاهدة به بالجامع المشترك الذي يجعلونه كلياً. فإن لم يكن هذا صحيحاً لم يكن مع أحد من أهل الأرض علم كلي يشترك فيه ما شهده وما غاب عنه، حتى قوله : «الخبز يشبع و الماء يروي ونحو ذلك . فإنه لم يعلم بحسه إلا أموراً معينة، فمن أين له أن الغائب بمنزلة الشاهد إلا بهذه الطريق؟ والإنسان قد ينكر أمراً حتى يرى واحداً جنسه ، فيقر بالنوع ويستفيد بذلك حكماً كلياً. ولهذا يقول سبحانه: ﴿ كَذَّبَتْ قَوْمُ [٣٦٠] نُوحٍ الْمُرْسَلِينَ، كَذَبَتْ عَادُ الْمُرْسَلِينَ، كَذَّبَتْ ثَمُودُ الْمُرْسَلِينَ ﴾ ، ونحو ذلك . وكلّ من هؤلاء إنما جاءه رسول واحد، لكن كانوا مكذبين بجنس الرسل بجنس الرُّسل لم يكن تكذيبهم بالواحد لخصوصه. وهذا بخلاف تكذيب اليهود والنصارى لمحمد صلى الله عليه وسلم فإنهم لم يكذبوا جنس الرسل، إنما كَذَّبوا واحداً بعينه. بخلاف مشركي العرب الذين لم يعرفوا الرسل، فإن الله يحتج عليهم في القرآن بإثبات جنس الرسالة . ولهذا يجيب سبحانه عن شُبَهِ منكري جنس الرسالة كقولهم : لو أَبَعَثَ الله بشرا رسولا [سورة الإسراء : ٩٤]، فيقول : ﴿وَمَا أَرْسَلْنَا مِن قَبْلِكَ إِلَّا رِجَالًا نُوحِيَ إِلَيْهِمْ فَسْتَلُوا أَهْلَ الذِكرِ إِن كُنتُمْ لَا تَعْلَمُونَ ﴾ [سورة النحل : ٤٣] . أي هذا متواتر عند أهل الكتاب، فاسئلوهم عن الرسل الذين جاءتهم أكانوا بشراً أم لا؟». وكذلك قوله : ﴿ وَقَالُوا لَوْلَا أُنزِلَ عَلَيْهِ مَلَكُ وَلَوْ أَنزَلْنَا مَلَكًا لَّقُضِيَ الْأَمْرُ ثُمَّ لَا يُنظَرُونَ ) وَلَوْ جَعَلْنَهُ مَلَكًا لَّجَعَلْتَهُ رَجُلًا وَلَلَبَسْنَا عَلَيْهِم مَّا يَلْبِسُونَ ﴾ [سورة الأنعام: ۸ - ۹] . فإنهم لا يُطيقون الأخذ عن الملك في صورته ، فلو أرسلنا إليهم مَلَكاً لجعلناه رجلاً في صورة الإنسان، وحينئذ كان يلتبس عليهم الأمرُ ويقولون هو رجل ، والرجل لا يكون رسولاً». وكذلك الرسل قبله. قال تعالى : ( أَوَعَبْتُمْ أَن جَاءَكُمْ ذِكْرٌ مِّن رَّبِّكُمْ عَلَى رَجُلٍ مِّنكُمْ لِيُنذِرَكُمْ) [سورة الأعراف : ٦٣] ، كما قال [٣٦١] تعالى: ﴿ أَكَانَ لِلنَّاسِ عَجَبًا أَنْ أَوْحَيْنَا إِلَى رَجُلٍ مِّنْهُمْ أَنْ أَنذِرِ النَّاسَ ﴾ [سورة يونس : ٢] وكما قال تعالى: ﴿قُلْ مَا كُنتُ بِدْعَا مِنَ الرُّسُلِ ﴾ [سورة الأحقاف: ٩]، ونحو ذلك.
The fourth station - the seventh aspect: Mentioning the principle to alert the intellect to the universal common. The universal common with some of its individuals is more established in the intellect than mentioning it devoid of all individuals, by agreement of the rational people. And therefore they say: The intellect, by virtue of its sensation of particulars, perceives among them a common universal quantity. So universals occur in the soul after knowledge of specific particulars. Knowledge of universals through specific particulars is among the greatest causes for knowledge of universals; so how can mentioning them weaken the syllogism, and not mentioning them be a cause for its strength? And this is a property of the intellect, for the property of the intellect is its knowledge of universals through its knowledge of particulars. So whoever denies this denies the property of the human intellect, and whoever makes mentioning them without any of their specific instances stronger than mentioning them with exemplification of their specific loci is being obstinate. The rational people unanimously know that striking a universal example assists in its knowledge, and that the case when it is mentioned with an example is not like the case when it is mentioned without an example. And whoever ponders all that people speak of regarding universals known by the intellect in medicine, examples for the universal of attraction of like and calculation and natural sciences and crafts and trades and other than that, finds the matter so. So if it is said: The interior of man becomes hot in winter and cold in summer, because in winter the air is cold so the exterior of the body cools and the heat flees to the interior of the body, for the opposite flees from the opposite, and the like is attracted to its similar, so coldness appears to the exterior because the similar of a thing is attracted to it - this would be an absolute universal matter. Then if it is said: Therefore the interior of the earth becomes hot in winter, and the interior of all animals, and therefore the interiors become cold in summer due to the heat of the exteriors so the coldness flees to the interiors - then whenever a person imagines the similars, his knowledge of that universal strengthens, i.e., that the opposite flees from its opposite and the like is attracted to its like. And this is known in natural and psychological matters and others. But when the similars are mentioned, knowledge of that is strengthened. And this is sometimes expressed by 'Homogeneity is the cause of [love?]'. Likewise, if it is said: The sun when it falls on the sea or other than it heats it so steam rises from it, an example of the rising of steam because heat dissolves moisture. Then it is said: Just as steam rises from the pot containing hot water - then this example strengthens knowledge of the first. And the syllogisms that the philosophers use in their sciences and make them universal - all of them they seek support in them by sensory evidence with examples. And the people have nothing except what they know of the attributes of observed matters, then they analogize the absent to the observed by the common factor that they make universal. For if this were not correct, there would be with no one on earth a universal knowledge that encompasses what he observed and what is absent from him, even his statement: 'Bread satiates and water quenches' and so on. For he only knows by his sensation specific matters; so from where does he have that the absent is like the observed except by this method? And a person may deny a matter until he sees one of its kind, then he acknowledges the type and thereby benefits a universal judgment. And therefore Allah Almighty says: 'The people of Noah denied the messengers, 'Ad denied the messengers, Thamud denied the messengers' and so on. And each of these was only sent one messenger, but they were deniers of the genus of messengers; their denial was not of the one for his specificity. This is unlike the denial of the Jews and Christians of Muhammad صلى الله عليه وسلم, for they did not deny the genus of messengers, they only denied one specific one. Unlike the polytheist Arabs who did not know messengers, for Allah argues against them in the Qur'an by establishing the genus of messengerhood. And therefore He answers the doubts of the deniers of the genus of messengerhood, like their statement: 'If Allah had sent a human as a messenger' [Surah al-Isra 94], He says 'And We sent not before you except men whom We inspired - so ask the people of remembrance if you do not know' [Surah al-Nahl 43]. That is, this is mutawatir among the People of the Book, so ask them about the messengers who came to them, were they human or not? And likewise His statement: 'And they said: Why was there not sent down to him an angel? And if We had sent down an angel, the matter would have been decided and then they would not be reprieved. And if We had made him an angel, We would have made him a man and We would have confused for them what they confuse' [Surah al-An'am 8-9]. For they cannot receive from an angel in its form; if We had sent them an angel, We would have made him a man in the form of a human, and then the matter would be confused for them and they would say he is a man, and a man cannot be a messenger. And likewise the messengers before him. He said: 'Is it a wonder for people that We inspired a man from among them to warn the people?' [Surah Yunus 2]. And as He said: 'Say: I am not an innovation among the messengers' [Surah al-Ahqaf 9], and so on.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage is a critical argument against the logicians' claim that mentioning examples weakens the syllogism. Ibn Taymiyya opens by stating that a universal common (المشترك الكلي) when accompanied by some of its individuals is more firmly established in the intellect than when mentioned in isolation. He then explains that the intellect grasps universals by first sensing particulars; thus, universals follow knowledge of specific individuals. Therefore, mentioning particulars cannot weaken the syllogism; rather, it strengthens it. He calls those who claim the opposite as obstinate (مكابر). He provides examples from natural phenomena: the movement of heat and cold in bodies, and the rise of steam from heated water. He also cites the use of examples in various fields like medicine, calculation, and crafts. Next, he argues that the philosophers' syllogisms rely on observed examples; all universal knowledge depends on extrapolating from the observed to the absent. Without this method, even basic knowledge like 'bread satiates' would be impossible. Finally, he uses a scriptural example: the denial of a single messenger by past nations constitutes denial of the genus of messengers (جنس الرسل), showing that the universal genus is known through the particular instance. This reinforces his point that universal knowledge is achieved through particulars and examples.

Checkpoint
What does Ibn Taymiyya mean by saying that even 'bread satiates' depends on this method?
A) That the statement is uncertain.
B) That knowledge that bread satiates comes from observing specific instances, not from a priori reasoning.
C) That bread satiates only in the presence of examples.
D) That the logicians deny bread satiates.

Key Takeaway
All universal knowledge, even the most mundane, is built on observation of particulars; there is no purely rational knowledge independent of experience.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: Take the statement 'Every prayer requires purification' which is a universal claim. List three particular instances that support this claim (e.g., the Prophet's practice, Qur'anic verses, consensus). Explain how these particulars make the universal more credible.

6 min
The Scriptural Example: Denial of the Genus of Messengers
Ibn Taymiyya uses Qur'anic examples to show that universal judgments arise from particulars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how Ibn Taymiyya uses a scriptural example to illustrate that the denial of a particular messenger often constitutes denial of the genus of messengers, thereby applying his epistemological principle to revelation.

Core Idea
The Qur'an treats denial of a single messenger as denial of the whole genus, confirming that universal judgments are made through particulars.

Ibn Taymiyya concludes his argument with a powerful scriptural illustration. He shows that when past nations denied their specific messenger, Allah described them as denying all messengers (جنس الرسل). This demonstrates that a particular instance serves as the basis for a universal judgment.

Guided Path
1
Locate the scriptural citation
Find the verses Ibn Taymiyya quotes: 'كَذَّبَتْ قَوْمُ نُوحٍ الْمُرْسَلِينَ' etc. These are from the Qur'an.
He uses multiple examples: Noah, 'Ad, Thamud.
2
Analyze his interpretation
He says each of these nations only received one messenger, yet Allah says they denied 'the messengers'. Why? Because they denied the genus of messengers through their denial of the particular.
The particular instance (the messenger) represents the genus.
3
Contrast with the Jews and Christians
The Jews and Christians denied Muhammad specifically, but not the genus of messengers. They accepted previous messengers.
This shows that denial can be of a specific individual, not necessarily the genus.
4
Connect to the main argument
How does this support Ibn Taymiyya's epistemological claim? The universal judgment (denial of all messengers) is derived from a particular (denial of one messenger). Examples are essential.
The Qur'an itself uses this method, validating Ibn Taymiyya's position.

المقام الرابع - الوجه السابع : ذكر الأصل لتنبيه العقل على المشترك الكلي المشترك مع بعض أفراده أثبتُ في العقل من ذكره مجرداً عن جميع الأفراد باتفاق العقلاء. ولهذا هم يقولون : إن العقل بحسب إحساسه [٣٥٨] بالجزئيات يدرك العقل بينها قدراً مشتركاً كلياً. فالكليات في النفس تقع بعد معرفة الجزئيات المعيَّنة. فمعرفة الكليات الجزئيات المعينة من أعظم الأسباب في معرفة الكليات فكيف يكون ذكرها مضعفاً للقياس، ويكون عدم ذكرها موجباً لقوته؟ وهذه خاصة العقل، فإن خاصة العقل معرفته الكليات بتوسط معرفته بالجزئيات فمن أنكرها أنكر خاصة عقل الإنسان، ومن جعل ذكرها بدون شيء من محالها المعينة أقوى من ذكرها مع التمثيل لمواضعها المعينة كان مكابراً. والعقلاء باتفاقهم يعلمون أن ضرب المثل الكلي مما يعين على معرفته، وأنه ليس الحال إذا ذكر مع المثال كالحال إذا ذكر مجرداً عن المثال . ومن تدبر جميع ما يتكلم فيه الناس من الكليات المعلومة بالعقل في الطب، أمثلة لكلية انجذاب النظير والحساب والطبيعيات والصناعات والتجارات وغير ذلك، وجد الأمر كذلك. فإذا قيل : يَسْخُن جوف الإنسان في الشتاء ويبرد في الصيف، لأنه في الشتاء يكون الهواء بارداً فيبرد ظاهرُ البدن فتهرب الحرارة إلى باطن البدن، لأن الضد يهرب من الضد، والنظير ينجذب إلى شبيهه، فتظهر البرودة إلى الظاهر، لأن شبيه الشيء منجذب إليه - كان هذا أمراً كلياً مطلقاً فإذا قيل : ولهذا يَسْخُن جوفُ الأرض في الشتاء، [٣٥٩] وجوف الحيوان كله، ولهذا تبرد الأجواف في الصيف لسخونة الظواهر فتهرب البرودة إلى الأجواف - كان كلما تصور الإنسان النظائر قويت معرفته بتلك الكلية، وهو أن الضد يهرب من ضده والنظير ينجذب إلى نظيره. وهذا معلوم في الطبيعيات والنفسانيات وغيرهما. لكن إذا ذكرت النظائر قوي العلم بذلك. وقد يعبر عن ذلك بأن «الجنسية علة القم. [احتمال: علة الحب]». وكذلك إذا قيل : الشمس إذا وقعت على البحر أو غيره سَخَّنته فتصاعد منه بخار، مثال تصاعد البخار لأن الحرارة تحلل الرطوبة. ثم قيل : كما يتصاعد البخار من القدر التي فيها الماء الحار - / كان هذا المثال مما يؤكد معرفة الأول. والأقيسة التي يستعملها الفلاسفة في علومهم ويجعلونها كلية كلُّها يعتضدون فيها على الشاهد بالأمثلة. وليس مع القوم إلا ما علموه من صفات الأمور المشاهدة، ثم قاسوا الغائب على المشاهدة به بالجامع المشترك الذي يجعلونه كلياً. فإن لم يكن هذا صحيحاً لم يكن مع أحد من أهل الأرض علم كلي يشترك فيه ما شهده وما غاب عنه، حتى قوله : «الخبز يشبع و الماء يروي ونحو ذلك . فإنه لم يعلم بحسه إلا أموراً معينة، فمن أين له أن الغائب بمنزلة الشاهد إلا بهذه الطريق؟ والإنسان قد ينكر أمراً حتى يرى واحداً جنسه ، فيقر بالنوع ويستفيد بذلك حكماً كلياً. ولهذا يقول سبحانه: ﴿ كَذَّبَتْ قَوْمُ [٣٦٠] نُوحٍ الْمُرْسَلِينَ، كَذَبَتْ عَادُ الْمُرْسَلِينَ، كَذَّبَتْ ثَمُودُ الْمُرْسَلِينَ ﴾ ، ونحو ذلك . وكلّ من هؤلاء إنما جاءه رسول واحد، لكن كانوا مكذبين بجنس الرسل بجنس الرُّسل لم يكن تكذيبهم بالواحد لخصوصه. وهذا بخلاف تكذيب اليهود والنصارى لمحمد صلى الله عليه وسلم فإنهم لم يكذبوا جنس الرسل، إنما كَذَّبوا واحداً بعينه. بخلاف مشركي العرب الذين لم يعرفوا الرسل، فإن الله يحتج عليهم في القرآن بإثبات جنس الرسالة . ولهذا يجيب سبحانه عن شُبَهِ منكري جنس الرسالة كقولهم : لو أَبَعَثَ الله بشرا رسولا [سورة الإسراء : ٩٤]، فيقول : ﴿وَمَا أَرْسَلْنَا مِن قَبْلِكَ إِلَّا رِجَالًا نُوحِيَ إِلَيْهِمْ فَسْتَلُوا أَهْلَ الذِكرِ إِن كُنتُمْ لَا تَعْلَمُونَ ﴾ [سورة النحل : ٤٣] . أي هذا متواتر عند أهل الكتاب، فاسئلوهم عن الرسل الذين جاءتهم أكانوا بشراً أم لا؟». وكذلك قوله : ﴿ وَقَالُوا لَوْلَا أُنزِلَ عَلَيْهِ مَلَكُ وَلَوْ أَنزَلْنَا مَلَكًا لَّقُضِيَ الْأَمْرُ ثُمَّ لَا يُنظَرُونَ ) وَلَوْ جَعَلْنَهُ مَلَكًا لَّجَعَلْتَهُ رَجُلًا وَلَلَبَسْنَا عَلَيْهِم مَّا يَلْبِسُونَ ﴾ [سورة الأنعام: ۸ - ۹] . فإنهم لا يُطيقون الأخذ عن الملك في صورته ، فلو أرسلنا إليهم مَلَكاً لجعلناه رجلاً في صورة الإنسان، وحينئذ كان يلتبس عليهم الأمرُ ويقولون هو رجل ، والرجل لا يكون رسولاً». وكذلك الرسل قبله. قال تعالى : ( أَوَعَبْتُمْ أَن جَاءَكُمْ ذِكْرٌ مِّن رَّبِّكُمْ عَلَى رَجُلٍ مِّنكُمْ لِيُنذِرَكُمْ) [سورة الأعراف : ٦٣] ، كما قال [٣٦١] تعالى: ﴿ أَكَانَ لِلنَّاسِ عَجَبًا أَنْ أَوْحَيْنَا إِلَى رَجُلٍ مِّنْهُمْ أَنْ أَنذِرِ النَّاسَ ﴾ [سورة يونس : ٢] وكما قال تعالى: ﴿قُلْ مَا كُنتُ بِدْعَا مِنَ الرُّسُلِ ﴾ [سورة الأحقاف: ٩]، ونحو ذلك.
The fourth station - the seventh aspect: Mentioning the principle to alert the intellect to the universal common. The universal common with some of its individuals is more established in the intellect than mentioning it devoid of all individuals, by agreement of the rational people. And therefore they say: The intellect, by virtue of its sensation of particulars, perceives among them a common universal quantity. So universals occur in the soul after knowledge of specific particulars. Knowledge of universals through specific particulars is among the greatest causes for knowledge of universals; so how can mentioning them weaken the syllogism, and not mentioning them be a cause for its strength? And this is a property of the intellect, for the property of the intellect is its knowledge of universals through its knowledge of particulars. So whoever denies this denies the property of the human intellect, and whoever makes mentioning them without any of their specific instances stronger than mentioning them with exemplification of their specific loci is being obstinate. The rational people unanimously know that striking a universal example assists in its knowledge, and that the case when it is mentioned with an example is not like the case when it is mentioned without an example. And whoever ponders all that people speak of regarding universals known by the intellect in medicine, examples for the universal of attraction of like and calculation and natural sciences and crafts and trades and other than that, finds the matter so. So if it is said: The interior of man becomes hot in winter and cold in summer, because in winter the air is cold so the exterior of the body cools and the heat flees to the interior of the body, for the opposite flees from the opposite, and the like is attracted to its similar, so coldness appears to the exterior because the similar of a thing is attracted to it - this would be an absolute universal matter. Then if it is said: Therefore the interior of the earth becomes hot in winter, and the interior of all animals, and therefore the interiors become cold in summer due to the heat of the exteriors so the coldness flees to the interiors - then whenever a person imagines the similars, his knowledge of that universal strengthens, i.e., that the opposite flees from its opposite and the like is attracted to its like. And this is known in natural and psychological matters and others. But when the similars are mentioned, knowledge of that is strengthened. And this is sometimes expressed by 'Homogeneity is the cause of [love?]'. Likewise, if it is said: The sun when it falls on the sea or other than it heats it so steam rises from it, an example of the rising of steam because heat dissolves moisture. Then it is said: Just as steam rises from the pot containing hot water - then this example strengthens knowledge of the first. And the syllogisms that the philosophers use in their sciences and make them universal - all of them they seek support in them by sensory evidence with examples. And the people have nothing except what they know of the attributes of observed matters, then they analogize the absent to the observed by the common factor that they make universal. For if this were not correct, there would be with no one on earth a universal knowledge that encompasses what he observed and what is absent from him, even his statement: 'Bread satiates and water quenches' and so on. For he only knows by his sensation specific matters; so from where does he have that the absent is like the observed except by this method? And a person may deny a matter until he sees one of its kind, then he acknowledges the type and thereby benefits a universal judgment. And therefore Allah Almighty says: 'The people of Noah denied the messengers, 'Ad denied the messengers, Thamud denied the messengers' and so on. And each of these was only sent one messenger, but they were deniers of the genus of messengers; their denial was not of the one for his specificity. This is unlike the denial of the Jews and Christians of Muhammad صلى الله عليه وسلم, for they did not deny the genus of messengers, they only denied one specific one. Unlike the polytheist Arabs who did not know messengers, for Allah argues against them in the Qur'an by establishing the genus of messengerhood. And therefore He answers the doubts of the deniers of the genus of messengerhood, like their statement: 'If Allah had sent a human as a messenger' [Surah al-Isra 94], He says 'And We sent not before you except men whom We inspired - so ask the people of remembrance if you do not know' [Surah al-Nahl 43]. That is, this is mutawatir among the People of the Book, so ask them about the messengers who came to them, were they human or not? And likewise His statement: 'And they said: Why was there not sent down to him an angel? And if We had sent down an angel, the matter would have been decided and then they would not be reprieved. And if We had made him an angel, We would have made him a man and We would have confused for them what they confuse' [Surah al-An'am 8-9]. For they cannot receive from an angel in its form; if We had sent them an angel, We would have made him a man in the form of a human, and then the matter would be confused for them and they would say he is a man, and a man cannot be a messenger. And likewise the messengers before him. He said: 'Is it a wonder for people that We inspired a man from among them to warn the people?' [Surah Yunus 2]. And as He said: 'Say: I am not an innovation among the messengers' [Surah al-Ahqaf 9], and so on.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage is a critical argument against the logicians' claim that mentioning examples weakens the syllogism. Ibn Taymiyya opens by stating that a universal common (المشترك الكلي) when accompanied by some of its individuals is more firmly established in the intellect than when mentioned in isolation. He then explains that the intellect grasps universals by first sensing particulars; thus, universals follow knowledge of specific individuals. Therefore, mentioning particulars cannot weaken the syllogism; rather, it strengthens it. He calls those who claim the opposite as obstinate (مكابر). He provides examples from natural phenomena: the movement of heat and cold in bodies, and the rise of steam from heated water. He also cites the use of examples in various fields like medicine, calculation, and crafts. Next, he argues that the philosophers' syllogisms rely on observed examples; all universal knowledge depends on extrapolating from the observed to the absent. Without this method, even basic knowledge like 'bread satiates' would be impossible. Finally, he uses a scriptural example: the denial of a single messenger by past nations constitutes denial of the genus of messengers (جنس الرسل), showing that the universal genus is known through the particular instance. This reinforces his point that universal knowledge is achieved through particulars and examples.

Key Terms
جنس الرسل
المشترك الكلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because they denied all messengers implicitly.
B) Because they denied the genus of messengers through their denial of the particular messenger.
C) Because they denied the concept of messengership.
D) Because they denied multiple messengers.

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an itself demonstrates that universal judgments are formed on the basis of particular instances, supporting Ibn Taymiyya's epistemological argument.

Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Analogical Reasoning (Qiyas al-Gha'ib)
Ibn Taymiyya critiques the logicians' reliance on analogical reasoning from the witnessed to the unseen.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and analyze Ibn Taymiyya's critique of analogical reasoning from the witnessed to the unseen, and evaluate its implications for universal knowledge claims.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya exposes the empirical limits of analogical reasoning, challenging its claim to universal certainty.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya takes aim at the logical method known as qiyas al-gha'ib, which the philosophers use to extend knowledge from observed matters to unseen ones via a universal commonality. He argues that this method is fundamentally flawed because it relies on particular empirical observations, not necessary truths. By examining his critique, you will sharpen your ability to assess the epistemic strength of analogical arguments in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target method
Locate the phrase 'qiyas al-gha'ib' in the Arabic. What does it mean? The logicians use it to reason from the witnessed (shahid) to the unseen (gha'ib) via a shared property they treat as universal.
The passage says: 'they analogize the absent to the witnessed by that shared commonality which they make universal.'
2
Extract Ibn Taymiyya's core objection
He says the logicians have only 'what they know from the attributes of observed matters.' Their universal knowledge is built on particular sense experiences. Therefore, the universal claim is not certain.
He questions: 'If this is not correct, then there is no one among the people of the earth with any universal knowledge...'
3
Analyze the example 'bread satiates'
Ibn Taymiyya uses this everyday statement to illustrate his point. We know from sense experience that a particular piece of bread satiates. But how do we know that all bread satiates, especially unseen bread? The universal judgment relies on analogical reasoning from the observed to the unobserved.
He asks: 'So from where does he have that the absent is like the witnessed except through this method?'
4
Recognize the epistemic consequence
If the logicians' method is unsound, then their claim to universal knowledge collapses. Ibn Taymiyya's critique has a sweeping implication: no one can claim certain universal knowledge based solely on empirical analogies.
This includes not only theological but also ordinary empirical generalizations.
5
Evaluate the critique's strength
Consider whether Ibn Taymiyya's argument is valid. He identifies the problem of induction: particular observations cannot guarantee universal truths. But does he offer an alternative foundation for universal knowledge? The passage does not provide one, leaving room for further debate.
This is a classic philosophical challenge that continues to be discussed in epistemology and usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرد على المنطقيين قياس الغائب والأقيسة التي يستعملها الفلاسفة في علومهم ويجعلونها كلية كلُّها يعتضدون فيها على الشاهد بالأمثلة. وليس مع القوم إلا ما علموه من صفات الأمور المشاهدة، ثم قاسوا الغائب على المشاهدة به بالجامع المشترك الذي يجعلونه كلياً. فإن لم يكن هذا صحيحاً لم يكن مع أحد من أهل الأرض علم كلي يشترك فيه ما شَهِده وما غاب عنه، حتى قوله : «الخبز يشبع و الماء يروي ونحو ذلك . فإنه لم يعلم بحسه إلا أموراً معينة، فمن أين له أن الغائب بمنزلة الشاهد إلا بهذه الطريق؟ والإنسان قد ينكر أمراً حتى يَرَى واحداً جنسه ، فيُقر بالنوع ويستفيد بذلك حكماً كلياً.
The book 'Refutation of the Logicians'. Analogical reasoning from the absent (qiyas al-gha'ib) and the syllogisms that the philosophers use in their sciences, making them universal, all of them relying in them on the witnessed by examples. And the people have nothing except what they know from the attributes of observed matters, then they analogize the absent to the witnessed by that shared commonality which they make universal. If this is not correct, then there is no one among the people of the earth with any universal knowledge that includes what he witnessed and what is absent from him, even his statement: 'Bread satiates, water quenches, and the like.' For he knows by his senses only specific matters, so from where does he have that the absent is like the witnessed except through this method? And a person may deny a thing until he sees one of its kind, then he acknowledges the species and thereby derives a universal judgment.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage opens with a critique of the logical method known as qiyas al-gha'ib (analogical reasoning from the witnessed to the unseen). Ibn Taymiyya argues that the philosophers rely on this type of reasoning to establish universal propositions. They use examples from the witnessed world (shahid) and apply them to the unseen (gha'ib) via a universal commonality. He then points out that if this method is not sound, then no universal knowledge exists, because all such knowledge is based on empirical observations of particular instances. He gives the example of 'bread satiates' – we only know that particular bread satiates, and we generalize to all bread. The universal judgment comes from seeing one individual of a species and inferring the species' property. This is a fundamental critique of the logical foundation of analogical reasoning.

Key Terms

شاهد
غائب
كلي

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's critique reveals that universal knowledge claims built on analogical reasoning from the witnessed to the unseen lack certain epistemic foundation because they depend on particular empirical observations.

Rejecting One Messenger vs. Rejecting the Genus
Ibn Taymiyya's logical critique of denying prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between rejecting a specific messenger and rejecting the entire class of messengers, using Ibn Taymiyya's logical criterion.

Core Idea
Denial of a messenger often reflects denial of the very institution of prophethood.

Ibn Taymiyya uses Quranic verses to argue that when polytheists rejected a messenger because he was human, they were not just denying that person but the entire concept of human messengers. This lesson unpacks that logical distinction and its significance for defending prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Types of Denial
Read the Quranic examples: the people of Noah, 'Ad, and Thamud each had one messenger but are accused of denying 'the messengers' (plural). Notice the contrast with Jews and Christians who deny Muhammad specifically while accepting the institution.
The passage labels the first type as denial of the genus (jins al-rusul), the second as denial of a particular (mu'ayyan).
2
Analyze the Grounds of Denial
The polytheists objected to human messengers. Their reason — 'Why was a human sent?' — applies to any human messenger, not just the one. This shows their denial targets the type, not the individual.
Ibn Taymiyya cites Quran 17:94 and 6:8-9 to show the objection is about the genus.
3
Contrast with Jews and Christians
Jews and Christians believed in messengers but rejected Muhammad (salla Allahu alayhi wasallam). Their denial is of a specific person, not the type. The passage uses this to clarify the logical difference.
This distinction helps in responding to different kinds of objections.
4
Examine the Logical Principle
Ibn Taymiyya states that knowing one particular messenger (e.g., Noah) establishes the existence of the genus. This is an inductive inference: one instance confirms the type more strongly than a hypothetical initial claim.
He uses Noah as the first messenger to show how a concrete example makes the abstract type more evident.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهذا يقول سبحانه: ﴿ كَذَّبَتْ قَوْمُ نُوحٍ الْمُرْسَلِينَ، كَذَبَتْ عَادُ الْمُرْسَلِينَ، كَذَّبَتْ ثَمُودُ الْمُرْسَلِينَ ﴾ ، ونحو ذلك . وكلّ من هؤلاء إنما جاءه رسول واحد، لكن كانوا مكذبين بجنس الرسل بجنس الرُّسل لم يكن تكذيبهم بالواحد لخصوصه. وهذا بخلاف تكذيب اليهود والنصارى لمحمد صلى الله عليه وسلم فإنهم لم يكذبوا جنس الرسل، إنما كَذَّبوا واحداً بعينه. بخلاف مشركي العرب الذين لم يعرفوا الرسل، فإن الله يحتج عليهم في القرآن بإثبات جنس الرسالة . ولهذا يجيب سبحانه عن شُبَهِ منكري جنس الرسالة كقولهم : لو أَبَعَثَ الله بشرا رسولا ﴾ [سورة الإسراء : ٩٤]، فيقول : ﴿وَمَا أَرْسَلْنَا مِن قَبْلِكَ إِلَّا رِجَالًا نُوحِيَ إِلَيْهِمْ فَسْتَلُوا أَهْلَ الذِكرِ إِن كُنتُمْ لَا تَعْلَمُونَ ﴾ [سورة النحل : ٤٣] . أي هذا متواتر عند أهل الكتاب، فاسئلوهم عن الرسل الذين جاءتهم أكانوا بشراً أم لا؟». وكذلك قوله : ﴿ وَقَالُوا لَوْلَا أُنزِلَ عَلَيْهِ مَلَكُ وَلَوْ أَنزَلْنَا مَلَكًا لَّقُضِيَ الْأَمْرُ ثُمَّ لَا يُنظَرُونَ ) وَلَوْ جَعَلْنَهُ مَلَكًا لَّجَعَلْتَهُ رَجُلًا وَلَلَبَسْنَا عَلَيْهِم مَّا يَلْبِسُونَ ﴾ [سورة الأنعام: ۸ - ۹] . فإنهم لا يُطيقون الأخذ عن الملك في صورته ، فلو أرسلنا إليهم مَلَكاً لجعلناه رجلاً في صورة الإنسان، وحينئذ كان يلتبس عليهم الأمرُ ويقولون هو رجل ، والرجل لا يكون رسولاً». وكذلك الرسل قبله. قال تعالى : ( أَوَعَبْتُمْ أَن جَاءَكُمْ ذِكْرٌ مِّن رَّبِّكُمْ عَلَى رَجُلٍ مِّنكُمْ لِيُنذِرَكُمْ) [سورة الأعراف : ٦٣] ، كما قال [٣٦١] تعالى: ﴿ أَكَانَ لِلنَّاسِ عَجَبًا أَنْ أَوْحَيْنَا إِلَى رَجُلٍ مِّنْهُمْ أَنْ أَنذِرِ النَّاسَ ﴾ [سورة يونس : ٢] وكما قال تعالى: ﴿قُلْ مَا كُنتُ بِدْعَا مِنَ الرُّسُلِ ﴾ [سورة الأحقاف: ٩]، ونحو ذلك . المقام الرابع - الوجه السابع : العلم ببعض الرسل يوجب وجود جنس الرسل فكان علمهم بثبوتِ معيّن من هذا النوع يوجب العلم بقضية مطلقة، وهو أن هذا إثبات النوع بثبوت النظير النوع موجود ؛ بخلاف ما إذا أثبت ذلك ابتداءً بلا وجود نظير، فإنه يكون أصعب وإن كان ممكناً . فإن نوحاً أول رسول بعثه الله إلى أهل الأرض، ولم يكن قبله رسول بعث إلى الكفار المشركين يدعوهم إلى الانتقال عن الشرك إلى التوحيد وآدم والذين كانوا بعده كان الناس نوح في زمنهم مسلمين كما قال ابن عباس : كان بين آدم ونوح عشرة قرون كلهم على الإسلام لكن لَمَّا بعث الله نوحاً وأنجى من آمن به وأهلك مَنْ كذبه صار هذا المعين يثبت هذا النوع أقوى مما كان يثبت ابتداءً .
And therefore He, glorified, says: 'The people of Noah denied the messengers, the people of 'Ad denied the messengers, Thamud denied the messengers' and the like. And each of these only had one messenger come to them, but they were deniers of the genus of messengers—their denial was not of the one specifically. This is contrary to the denial of the Jews and Christians of Muhammad, peace be upon him, for they did not deny the genus of messengers, but they denied one specific individual. Contrary to the Arab polytheists who did not know messengers, for Allah argues against them in the Quran by affirming the genus of messengerhood. And for this reason He, glorified, responds to the doubts of deniers of the genus of messengerhood, like their saying: 'If Allah had sent a human as a messenger' (al-Isra 94), He says: 'And We sent not before you any but men to whom We revealed—so ask the people of the Reminder if you do not know' (al-Nahl 43). i.e., this is well-known among the People of the Book, so ask them about the messengers who came to them, were they human or not? And also His saying: 'They said: Why has not an angel been sent down to him? If We had sent down an angel, the matter would have been decided, and then they would not be reprieved. And if We had made him an angel, We would have made him a man, and We would have confused for them what they are confusing' (al-An'am 8-9). For they cannot receive from an angel in his form, so if We sent to them an angel, We would have made him a man in human form, and then the matter would be confused for them, and they would say he is a man, and a man cannot be a messenger. And likewise the messengers before him. He, glorified, says: 'Are you astonished that a reminder from your Lord has come to you upon a man from among you to warn you' (al-A'raf 63), as He, glorified, says: 'Is it a wonder to mankind that We revealed to a man from among them that he warn the people?' (Yunus 2), and as He says: 'Say: I am not an innovation among the messengers' (al-Ahqaf 9), and the like. The Fourth Station - The Seventh Aspect: The knowledge of some messengers entails the existence of the genus of messengers. So their knowledge of the establishment of a particular of this type entails knowledge of an absolute proposition, which is that this is an affirmation of the type by establishing a similar type that exists; contrary to if one establishes that initially without an existing peer, for it is more difficult though possible. For Noah was the first messenger sent by Allah to the people of the earth, and there was no messenger before him sent to the polytheist disbelievers calling them to move from shirk to tawhid, and Adam and those after him—the people in Noah's time were Muslims, as Ibn 'Abbas said: 'Between Adam and Noah there were ten centuries, all of them upon Islam.' But when Allah sent Noah and saved those who believed in him and destroyed those who denied him, this particular made this type stronger than it was when established initially.

Commentary
This passage is a critical analysis of the logical implication of rejecting a single messenger. Ibn Taymiyya uses Quranic evidence to show that when people deny a specific messenger because they reject the very idea of messengers (the type), their denial applies to all messengers. He contrasts this with those who deny a particular messenger while accepting the institution of messengerhood, like the Jews and Christians denying Muhammad. He then explains the Quranic response to those who object to human messengers, citing several verses to affirm the genus of messengerhood. Finally, he introduces a logical point: knowing one particular messenger (e.g., Noah) establishes the existence of the type (genus) of messengerhood, and this is stronger than establishing it initially without a previous example. He uses Noah as an example because he was the first messenger; his existence made the type more firmly established.

Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of the 'One from One' Principle
Ibn Taymiyya refutes the philosophical principle that from one only one can proceed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's two-part critique of the principle 'the one does not issue from the one' and identify its historical origins in Mu'tazili thought.

Core Idea
The 'one from one' principle fails because even natural causes need a receptive subject.

This lesson examines Ibn Taymiyya's incisive critique of a cornerstone of Neoplatonic metaphysics: the principle that from a single, simple cause only one effect can directly proceed. You will learn how he dismantles this principle on two fronts—first by showing its origin in flawed natural observation, and second by exposing its philosophical argument as borrowed from Mu'tazili theology rather than from the early Greek philosophers. By the end, you will be able to apply this critique to similar claims about divine unity and causality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle under attack
Locate the exact phrase 'الواحد لا يصدر عنه إلا واحد' in the Arabic text. This is the Neoplatonic principle that from a single simple cause only one effect can directly proceed.
Ibn Taymiyya does not reject the statement outright in all contexts, but he criticizes its universal application.
2
Analyze the natural example and its flaw
Ibn Taymiyya quotes the natural example: the cold only necessitates cooling, the hot only heating. He then points out that even here, the effect (coldness) requires a receptive subject and removal of obstacles. Hence the cause does not act alone—it requires two things, not one.
This shows that even in the physical world, the principle does not hold as stated.
3
Trace the philosophical argument to its source
Ibn Taymiyya identifies Ibn Sina's argument: if two effects issued from one cause, composition (tarkib) would result, contradicting unity. He claims this argument was taken from the Mu'tazila, not from the early philosophers like Aristotle.
This historical claim is central: the principle is not authentically philosophical but borrowed from mutakallimun.
4
Evaluate the critique of the principle
Ibn Taymiyya's critique is epistemological: the principle is not derived from revelation nor from sound reason. He points to earlier philosophers (like Abu al-Barakat) who affirmed divine attributes and voluntary actions, contradicting the principle.
The critique does not rely on rejecting logic wholesale but on showing the principle's limited scope.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذين قالوا: «الواحد لا يصدر عنه إلا واحد كان مبدأ كلامهم في الأمور الطبيعية. صدور الواحد عن الواحد فإنهم رأوا البارد إنما يقتضي التبريد فقط، والحار إنما يقتضي التسخين فقط، وكذلك سائرها. لكن هذا ليس فيه إحداث واحد لواحد، فإن البرودة الحاصلة لا بد لها مع السبب الطبيعية من محل قابل وارتفاع موانع فلم يحصل السبب إلا عن شيئين، لا عن واحد. لكن هذا كان مبدأ كلامهم . وأما احتجاج [٣٦٢] ابن سينا وأمثاله بأنه لو صدر اثنان لكان مصدر هذا غير مصدر حجة التركيب هذا، ولزم «التركيب المنافي للوحدة، فهذه الحجة تبع الحجة التركيب». وهذه أخذوها المعتزلة من أهل الكلام من المعتزلة ونحوهم، ليست هذه من كلام أئمة الفلاسفة كأرسطو وأتباعه، لا سيما أكثر أساطين الفلاسفة . فإنهم كانوا يقولون بإثبات الصفات الله تعالى، بل وبقيام الأمور الاختيارية، كما ذكرنا كلامهم في غير هذا الموضع وهو اختيار أبي البركات صاحب «المعتبر». ومن قال إنه خالف أكثرَ الفلاسفة فمراده المشائين . وأما الأساطين قبل هؤلاء فكلام كثير منهم يدل على هذا الأصل، كما هو مذكور في موضعه .
And those who said: 'The one does not issue from except one'—the beginning of their speech was in natural matters. The issuing of the one from the one. For they saw that the cold only necessitates cooling, and the hot only necessitates heating, and likewise the rest. But this does not involve producing one from one, for the coldness that occurs necessarily requires, along with the natural cause, a receptive subject and the removal of obstacles, so the cause does not result from two things, not from one. But this was the beginning of their speech. As for the argument of Ibn Sina and his likes that if two issued, then the source of this would be other than the source of that and composition would be necessary, and 'composition is incompatible with unity'—this argument follows the argument of composition. And they took this from the Mu'tazila, from the people of kalam and the like; this is not from the speech of the leading philosophers like Aristotle and his followers, especially most of the founders of philosophy. For they used to affirm attributes for Allah, and even the occurrence of voluntary matters, as we have mentioned their speech elsewhere, and it is the choice of Abu al-Barakat, author of al-Mu'tabar. And whoever says he opposed most philosophers, he means the Peripatetics. As for the founders before them, much of their speech indicates this principle, as is mentioned in its place.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage criticizes the famous philosophical principle that 'from the one only one can proceed' (al-wahid la yasdur 'anhu illa wahid). Ibn Taymiyya explains that this principle originated from observations in nature, such as that cold only produces cooling and heat only heating. However, he points out that even in natural causation, the effect requires more than just the cause—it needs a receptive subject and removal of obstacles, so the cause does not produce from one alone. He then attacks Ibn Sina's argument that if two proceeded from one, then composition would result, which contradicts unity. Ibn Taymiyya claims this argument was borrowed from the Mu'tazila and is not from the early philosophers like Aristotle. He notes that many earlier philosophers affirmed attributes and voluntary actions for God, supporting a more nuanced view.

Key Terms
الواحد لا يصدر عنه إلا واحد
التركيب
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, what is the flaw in the principle 'the one only issues from the one' based on natural examples?
A) Cold can produce heat
B) Causes require a receptive subject and removal of obstacles
C) One cause always produces many effects
D) The principle is from revelation

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's critique shows that the 'one from one' principle is neither empirically sound nor authentically Aristotelian, but a borrowed theological concept.

The Intellect's Recognition of Similarity and Qiyas al-Tard
Ibn Taymiyya describes the intellect's ability to recognize similarity and apply universal judgments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Ibn Taymiyya's epistemological grounding of qiyas al-tard in the intellect's direct perception of similarity and contrast it with formal analogical reasoning.

Core Idea
Qiyas al-tard is not a formal rule—it is the intellect’s natural recognition of similarity.

Ibn Taymiyya argues that the greatest function of the intellect is to perceive similarity and difference. In this passage, he grounds analogical reasoning (qiyas) in this innate cognitive ability, proposing that the strongest form of analogy is one that directly observes similarity. This shifts the focus from abstract logical forms to concrete intellectual perception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the intellect's primary function
Locate the phrase where Ibn Taymiyya states that 'among the greatest attributes of the intellect is the knowledge of similarity and difference.' This is the foundational claim.
2
Understand the water example
When the intellect sees two similar things like water and water, it naturally knows they are alike and applies a universal judgment to the common aspect. This is not inference but direct recognition.
The example illustrates how the intellect operates intuitively.
3
Define qiyas al-tard from the passage
Ibn Taymiyya says that if one judges based on observing similarity among individuals and then mentioning the commonality, that is qiyas al-tard. He calls this 'better in elucidation.'
Qiyas al-tard is thus a direct analogical move from observed similarity.
4
Contrast with standard analogical reasoning
Compare this with the formal usul al-fiqh definition of qiyas, which requires an explicit 'illa (effective cause). Ibn Taymiyya seems to bypass that, emphasizing raw perception of similarity.
This is a critique of overly formalized logic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن أعظم صفات العقل معرفة التماثل والاختلاف فإذا رأى الشيئين المماثلين علم أن هذا مثل هذا، فجعل حكمهما واحداً، كما إذا رأى الماء والماء والتراب والتراب والهواء والهواء، ثم حكم بالحكم الكلي على القدر المشترك. وإذا حكم على بعض معرفة التماثل الأعيان ومثله بالنظر وذكر المشترك كان أحسن في البيان . فهذا قياس الطَّرد». وإذا رأى والاختلاف
And among the greatest attributes of the intellect is the knowledge of similarity and difference. For when it sees two similar things, it knows that this is like that, so it makes their judgment one, as when it sees water and water, dirt and dirt, air and air, then it judges with a universal judgment on the common aspect. And if it judges on some instances of knowing the similarity of individuals and their like by consideration and mentioning the commonality, that is better in elucidation. This is qiyas al-tard (coextensive analogy). And when it sees and difference...
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage discusses the cognitive faculty of the intellect ('aql) in recognizing similarity and difference. Ibn Taymiyya states that one of the greatest functions of the intellect is to perceive when two things are alike. When it sees two similar things (e.g., water and water), it recognizes that they share a nature and thus applies a universal judgment to the common aspect. He explains that if the intellect judges based on observing similarity among individuals and then considers the commonality, it is a more excellent form of explanation. He calls this 'qiyas al-tard' (coextensive analogy or analogy of concomitance). The passage ends abruptly with 'and when it sees and difference,' indicating a discussion of how the intellect also recognizes difference in contrast to similarity.

الاختلاف

D) It withholds judgment

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya grounds analogical reasoning in the intellect's natural capacity to recognize similarity, not in formal logical rules.

Ibn Taymiyya on Cause and Effect: Rejecting Temporal Simultaneity
Ibn Taymiyya refutes the logicians' claim that cause and effect can be simultaneous.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Ibn Taymiyya's objection to the logicians' claim that cause and effect can be simultaneous in time, and distinguish temporal from intellectual priority.

Core Idea
Cause precedes effect intellectually, not temporally—a critical distinction for theology and fiqh.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya tackles a foundational issue: can cause and effect coexist in time? The logicians, and even some theologians, argued yes, using examples like hand and ring movement. Ibn Taymiyya refutes this, warning that misunderstanding leads to confusion in all intellectual disciplines. Let's walk through his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim under attack
What do the logicians assert? They claim that cause and effect can be simultaneous in time, using examples like hand/ring, sun/ray, motion/sound.
2
Examine their examples
The logicians' examples: hand moving a ring, sun emitting a ray, motion producing sound. In each, cause and effect appear together in time.
Ibn Taymiyya argues these only show intellectual priority, not temporal simultaneity.
3
Understand Ibn Taymiyya's counter
Ibn Taymiyya insists that cause precedes effect by intellectual priority (taqaddum 'aqli), meaning the cause is logically prior without necessarily being temporally prior. The examples are misinterpreted.
The key point: the cause is conceptually prior even if they occur together.
4
Trace the error's source
Ibn Taymiyya links this error to theologians who affirm 'states' (ahwal), like al-Qadi Abu Bakr and Abu al-Ma'ali, who considered knowledge as a cause for God's being knowing.
This led them to accept the idea of cause and effect being concomitant (mutalaziman).
5
Recognize the consequence
This error affected jurists like Abu al-Ma'ali, Abu Hamid al-Ghazali, and al-Rafi'i, causing them to contradict the consensus of earlier imams.
If cause and effect are simultaneous, one could argue the world is co-eternal with God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إبطال القول باقتران العلة والمعلول في الزمان

ولهذا من لم يُحكم معرفة هذا وإلا التبست عليه المعقولات ودخل عليه غلطهم - سواء كانوا قد غلطوا هم في التصور، وهو الغالب على أئمتهم؛ أو كانوا يقصدون التغليط، كما يفعله بعضهم. غلطهم جعل مثال ذلك: أنه إذا قيل لهم في مسئلة حدوث العالم: «كيف يكون العالم مفعولاً مصنوعاً للرب وهو مساوي له أزلاً وأبداً مقارن له في الزمان؟ هذا مما يعلم فساده بضرورة العقل، فإن المفعول لا يكون مقارناً للفاعل في الزمان» قالوا: بل هذا ممكن. وهو أن تقدم العلة على المعلول تقدماً عقلياً لازماً كتقدم حركة اليد على حركة الخاتم الذي فيها، وتقدم الشمس على الشعاع، وتقدم الحركة على الصوت الناشيء عنها. ثم إن كان ممن تكلم في العلة والمعلول المذكور في الصفات والأحوال، وهو يقول العلم علة كون العالم عالماً كما يقوله مثبتوا الأحوال من النظار، كالقاضي أبي بكر، وأبي المعالي في أول قوليه والقاضي أبي يعلى وأمثالهم، فإنه قد ألف أن العلة والمعلول متلازمان مقترنان فلا يستنكر مثل هذا هنا. ولهذا غلط بسبب متابعتهم في هذا طوائفُ من الفقهاء في الفقه، كأبي المعالي وأتباعه أبي حامد والرافعي وغيرهم. فادَّعوا شيئاً خالفوا فيه جميع أئمة الفقه.
Refutation of the statement about the simultaneity of cause and effect in time. For this reason, whoever does not master knowledge of this will have intelligibles confused for him and their error will enter upon him—whether they themselves erred in conception, as is predominant among their leaders, or they intended to mislead, as some do. Their error: taking as an example that when it is said to them in the issue of the temporal origination of the world: 'How can the world be an effect and a creation of the Lord while it is equal to Him eternally and everlastingly, concurrent with Him in time? This is known to be false by the necessity of reason, for the effect cannot be concurrent with the agent in time.' They say: 'Rather, this is possible. That is, the cause precedes the effect by a necessary intellectual priority, like the priority of the movement of the hand over the movement of the ring on it, and the priority of the sun over the ray, and the priority of the movement over the sound arising from it.' Then if the person is among those who spoke about cause and effect with regard to attributes and states, and he says that knowledge is the cause of the world being knowing, as the affirmers of states among the speculative theologians say, like al-Qadi Abu Bakr, and Abu al-Ma'ali in his first view, and al-Qadi Abu Ya'la and the like, he has become accustomed that cause and effect are concomitant and concurrent, so he does not find it objectionable here. For this reason, due to following them in this, groups of jurists in fiqh fell into error, like Abu al-Ma'ali and his followers Abu Hamid and al-Rafi'i and others. They claimed something in which they contradicted all the imams of fiqh.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation by Ibn Taymiyya of the logicians' and theologians' claim that cause and effect can be simultaneous in time. He begins by warning that failure to understand this leads to confusion. Then he presents the logicians' example: when asked how the world can be an effect of God while being co-eternal with Him, they respond that cause and effect can be simultaneous, using examples like hand and ring (movement), sun and ray, motion and sound. Ibn Taymiyya argues that these examples only show intellectual priority, not temporal simultaneity. He then connects this error to certain theologians who adopted the view that attributes like knowledge are causes of states, leading to the belief in concomitance. Finally, he blames this error for leading jurists like Abu al-Ma'ali, Abu Hamid al-Ghazali, and al-Rafi'i to contradict the consensus of jurists.

Key Terms
العلة والمعلول
تقدماً عقلياً
متلازمان
مثبتوا الأحوال

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The movement of the hand and the ring on it
B) The sun and the moon
C) Fire and burning
D) The agent and the act of writing

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya refutes the simultaneity of cause and effect by showing that the logicians' examples only prove intellectual priority, not temporal coexistence, and this error leads to contradictions in theology and fiqh.

Theological Background: No Efficient Cause in Divine Attributes
Ibn Taymiyya refutes the philosophers' claim that an efficient cause can be simultaneous with its effect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Ibn Taymiyya rejects the simultaneous efficient cause in divine attributes, and identify the equivocation on the term 'cause'.

Core Idea
The efficient cause must precede its effect; simultaneity indicates a condition, not a cause.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya launches a sharp critique against the philosophers who assert that an efficient cause can be simultaneous with its effect. He begins by clarifying the theological context: most rational thinkers—including Sunni and Mu'tazili theologians—reject cause-and-effect language when discussing divine attributes like knowledge. For them, there is no 'cause' producing the attribute; rather, the attribute is simply necessary. Ibn Taymiyya then pivots to the philosophers' examples, showing why they fail to demonstrate a simultaneous efficient cause. This lesson unpacks his theological foundations and the first part of his argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the theological position
Find where Ibn Taymiyya states that 'according to the majority of rational people, there is no cause and effect here; rather, knowledge is the attribute of being knowing.' What is the doctrine of the majority of speculative theologians?
They negate 'states' (ahwal) and deny a causal relation between the knower and the attribute of knowledge.
2
Understand the negation of states
He mentions that those who affirm 'states' consider them neither existent nor non-existent. Why does this make them unsuitable as effects?
Effects are existential, so non-existential states cannot be seen as existential effects.
3
Distinguish two senses of 'cause'
Ibn Taymiyya warns that the word 'cause' (علة) is ambiguous. He contrasts efficient cause (العلة الفاعلة) with condition (الشرط). Identify where he says 'the efficient cause is one thing, and the condition is another.'
4
Apply the distinction to divine attributes
Consider: in the case of God's knowledge, is His being knowing an effect of an efficient cause? According to Ibn Taymiyya, no―it is necessary, not caused. How does this differ from physical causes like cutting the neck causing death?
The former is a necessary concomitant of knowledge; the latter is a created cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عند جماهير العقلاء ليس هنا علةٌ ومعلول، بل العلم هو العالمية. وهذا مذهب جمهور نظار أهل السنة والبدعة، وهو نفي الأحوال، فلا علة ولا معلول. وإن جعلت المعلول الحكم بكونه عالماً» و «الخبر عنه بكونه عالماً فهذا قد يتأخر عن العلم. وعلى قول من أثبت الحال هو يقول : إنها ليست موجودة ولا معدومة فليست نظير المعلولات الوجودية . وأيضاً فهؤلاء يقولون : إن العالم فاعل للعالمية، ولا هو جاعل العالمية. ولا هذا عنده
